	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Human Development Index</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-fr-revisiontag" class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><span aria-disabled='false' title='Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page.' class='flaggedrevs-icon oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-articleSearch oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-iconWidget'></span><span id='mw-fr-revisiontoggle' aria-disabled='false' title='show/hide details' class='fr-toggle-arrow oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicator-down oo-ui-indicatorElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-indicatorWidget'></span></div>
<div id="mw-fr-revisiondetails-wrapper" style="position:relative;"><div id="mw-fr-revisiondetails" class="flaggedrevs_short_details" style="display:none">This is the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Pending_changes" title="Wikipedia:Pending changes">latest accepted revision</a>, <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:Log&amp;type=review&amp;page=Human_Development_Index">reviewed</a> on <i>15 September 2019</i>.</div>

		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"HDI" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/HDI_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="HDI (disambiguation)">HDI (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the complete ranking of countries, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">composite statistic of life expectancy, education, and income indices</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2018_HDI.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/2018_HDI.svg/450px-2018_HDI.svg.png" decoding="async" width="450" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/2018_HDI.svg/675px-2018_HDI.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/2018_HDI.svg/900px-2018_HDI.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2803" data-file-height="1333" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2018_HDI.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>World map of countries by Human Development Index categories in increments of 0.050 (based on 2017 data, published on 14 September 2018). <table border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="width:100%; background:none;">  <tbody><tr> <td valign="top"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFD215; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.600–0.649</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FFA83C; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.550–0.599</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF852F; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.500–0.549</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF5B00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.450–0.499</div> </td> <td valign="top"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.400–0.449</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #A70000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;≤ 0.399</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #808080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Data unavailable</div> </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div>
<p>The <b>Human Development Index</b> (<b>HDI</b>) is a  statistic composite index of <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> indicators, which are used to rank countries into four tiers of <a href="/wiki/Human_development_(humanity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Human development (humanity)">human development</a>. A country scores a higher HDI when the <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" class="mw-redirect" title="Life expectancy at birth">lifespan</a> is higher, the <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a> level is higher, and the gross national income <a href="/wiki/GNI_(PPP)_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GNI (PPP) per capita">GNI (PPP) per capita</a> is higher.  It was developed by Pakistani economist <a href="/wiki/Mahbub_ul_Haq" title="Mahbub ul Haq">Mahbub ul Haq</a>, with help from <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Ranis" title="Gustav Ranis">Gustav Ranis</a> of Yale University and <a href="/wiki/Meghnad_Desai" class="mw-redirect" title="Meghnad Desai">Meghnad Desai</a> of the London School of Economics, and was further used to measure a country's development by the United Nations Development Programme (<a href="/wiki/UNDP" class="mw-redirect" title="UNDP">UNDP</a>)'s Human Development Report Office.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2010 <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Report" title="Human Development Report">Human Development Report</a> introduced an <b><a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index</a></b> (IHDI). While the simple HDI remains useful, it stated that "the IHDI is the actual level of human development (accounting for <a href="/wiki/Social_inequality" title="Social inequality">inequality</a>)", and "the HDI can be viewed as an index of 'potential' human development (or the maximum IHDI that could be achieved if there were no inequality)". The index does not take into account several factors, such as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_wealth_per_adult" title="List of countries by wealth per adult">net wealth per capita</a> or the relative <a href="/wiki/Quality_(business)" title="Quality (business)">quality of goods</a> in a country. This situation tends to lower the ranking for some of the most advanced countries, such as the <a href="/wiki/G7" class="mw-redirect" title="G7">G7</a> members and others.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The index is based on the human development approach, developed by Amartya Sen, often framed in terms of whether people are <b>able to "be" and "do"</b> desirable things in life. Examples include—Being: well fed, sheltered, healthy; Doings: work, education, voting, participating in community life. The freedom of choice is central—someone choosing to be hungry (as during a religious <a href="/wiki/Fasting" title="Fasting">fast</a>) is quite different from someone who is hungry because they cannot afford to buy food, or because the country is in a <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg/180px-Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg/270px-Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg/360px-Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg 2x" data-file-width="397" data-file-height="404" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mahbub_ul_Haq" title="Mahbub ul Haq">Mahbub ul Haq</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amartya_Sen_,_c2000_(4379246038).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Amartya_Sen_%2C_c2000_%284379246038%29.jpg/180px-Amartya_Sen_%2C_c2000_%284379246038%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Amartya_Sen_%2C_c2000_%284379246038%29.jpg/270px-Amartya_Sen_%2C_c2000_%284379246038%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Amartya_Sen_%2C_c2000_%284379246038%29.jpg/360px-Amartya_Sen_%2C_c2000_%284379246038%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="529" data-file-height="414" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amartya_Sen_,_c2000_(4379246038).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a></div></div></div>
<p>The origins of the HDI are found in the annual Human Development Reports produced by the Human Development Report Office of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> (UNDP). These were devised and launched by Pakistani economist <a href="/wiki/Mahbub_ul_Haq" title="Mahbub ul Haq">Mahbub ul Haq</a> in 1990, and had the explicit purpose "to shift the focus of development economics from <a href="/wiki/National_income" class="mw-redirect" title="National income">national income</a> accounting to <a href="/wiki/People-centered_development" title="People-centered development">people-centered policies</a>". To produce the Human Development Reports, Mahbub ul Haq formed a group of development economists including <a href="/wiki/Paul_Streeten" title="Paul Streeten">Paul Streeten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frances_Stewart_(economist)" title="Frances Stewart (economist)">Frances Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Ranis" title="Gustav Ranis">Gustav Ranis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Griffin_(economist)" title="Keith Griffin (economist)">Keith Griffin</a>, Sudhir Anand, and <a href="/wiki/Meghnad_Desai" class="mw-redirect" title="Meghnad Desai">Meghnad Desai</a>. Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a> utilized Haq's work in his own work on human capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Haq believed that a simple composite measure of human development was needed to convince the public, academics, and politicians that they can and should evaluate development not only by economic advances but also improvements in human <a href="/wiki/Well-being" title="Well-being">well-being</a>.
</p>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:772px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HDI_explained_the_best_way.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2b/HDI_explained_the_best_way.png/770px-HDI_explained_the_best_way.png" decoding="async" width="770" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/2b/HDI_explained_the_best_way.png 1.5x" data-file-width="985" data-file-height="175" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HDI_explained_the_best_way.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The underlying principle behind the Human Development Index.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dimensions_and_calculation">Dimensions and calculation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Dimensions and calculation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="New_method_.282010_Index_onwards.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_method_(2010_Index_onwards)">New method (2010 Index onwards)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: New method (2010 Index onwards)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg/400px-2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg.png" decoding="async" width="400" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg/600px-2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg/800px-2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2436" data-file-height="1095" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2018_UN_Human_Development_Report.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>World map representing  Human Development Index categories (based on 2017 data, published in 2018).<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Development_Index_Trends_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Development_Index_Trends-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> <table border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="width:100%; background:none;">  <tbody><tr> <td valign="top"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00023a; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.800–1.000 (very high)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000074; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.700–0.799 (high)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0010c0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.555–0.699 (medium)</div> </td> <td valign="top"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #aabdef; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;0.350–0.554 (low)</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #a0a0a0; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Data unavailable</div> </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div>
<p>Published on 4 November 2010 (and updated on 10 June 2011), the <a href="/wiki/2010_Human_Development_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 Human Development Report">2010 Human Development Report</a> calculated the HDI combining three dimensions:<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>A long and healthy life: <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" class="mw-redirect" title="Life expectancy at birth">Life expectancy at birth</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Education_index" class="mw-redirect" title="Education index">Education index</a>: Mean years of schooling and Expected years of schooling</li>
<li>A decent standard of living: <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">GNI</a> per capita (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a> US$)</li></ul>
<p>In its 2010 Human Development Report, the UNDP began using a new method of calculating the HDI. The following three indices are used:
</p><p>1.<span id="Life_Expectancy_Index"></span> Life Expectancy Index (LEI) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle ={\frac {{\textrm {LE}}-20}{85-20}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>LE</mtext>
                </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mn>20</mn>
            </mrow>
            <mrow>
              <mn>85</mn>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mn>20</mn>
            </mrow>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle ={\frac {{\textrm {LE}}-20}{85-20}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a222c3bdfb22ca9ff86d4861b5a7a35fac63925d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:11.49ex; height:5.343ex;" alt="={\frac {{\textrm {LE}}-20}{85-20}}"/></span>
</p>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>LEI is 1 when <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" class="mw-redirect" title="Life expectancy at birth">Life expectancy at birth</a> is 85 and 0 when <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" class="mw-redirect" title="Life expectancy at birth">Life expectancy at birth</a> is 20.</dd></dl></dd></dl>
<p>2. <a href="/wiki/Education_Index" title="Education Index">Education Index</a> (EI) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle ={\frac {{\textrm {MYSI}}+{\textrm {EYSI}}}{2}}}">
  <semantics>

                </mrow>
              </mrow>

            <mn>2</mn>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle ={\frac {{\textrm {MYSI}}+{\textrm {EYSI}}}{2}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/322a300516420de9fa83acbd25f56e3f704e7ef8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:17.594ex; height:5.343ex;" alt="={\frac {{\textrm {MYSI}}+{\textrm {EYSI}}}{2}}"/></span><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd>2.1 Mean Years of Schooling Index (MYSI) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle ={\frac {\textrm {MYS}}{15}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<dl><dd>Fifteen is the projected maximum of this indicator for 2025.</dd></dl></dd>
<dd>2.2 Expected Years of Schooling Index (EYSI) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle ={\frac {\textrm {EYS}}{18}}}">

<dl><dd>Eighteen is equivalent to achieving a <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master&#39;s degree">master's degree</a> in most countries.</dd></dl></dd></dl>
<p>3. Income Index (II) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle ={\frac {\ln({\textrm {GNIpc}})-\ln(100)}{\ln(75,000)-\ln(100)}}}">

              <mn>100</mn>
              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
            </mrow>
            <mrow>

</p>
<dl><dd><dl><dd>II is 1 when GNI per capita is $75,000 and 0 when GNI per capita is $100.</dd></dl></dd></dl>
<p>Finally, the HDI is the <a href="/wiki/Geometric_mean" title="Geometric mean">geometric mean</a> of the previous three normalized indices:
</p><p><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\textrm {HDI}}={\sqrt[{3}]{{\textrm {LEI}}\cdot {\textrm {EI}}\cdot {\textrm {II}}}}.}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mtext>HDI</mtext>
          </mrow>
        </mrow>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mroot>
            <mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>LEI</mtext>
                </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>EI</mtext>
                </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>II</mtext>
                </mrow>
              </mrow>
            </mrow>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mn>3</mn>
            </mrow>
          </mroot>
        </mrow>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\textrm {HDI}}={\sqrt[{3}]{{\textrm {LEI}}\cdot {\textrm {EI}}\cdot {\textrm {II}}}}.}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/364ecd910bf260a13250cde6a9d25e08d9633fe8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:21.375ex; height:3.009ex;" alt="{\textrm {HDI}}={\sqrt[{3}]{{\textrm {LEI}}\cdot {\textrm {EI}}\cdot {\textrm {II}}}}."/></span>
</p><p><small>LE: <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" class="mw-redirect" title="Life expectancy at birth">Life expectancy at birth</a><br />
MYS: Mean years of schooling (i.e. years that a person aged 25 or older has spent in formal education)<br />
EYS: Expected years of schooling (i.e. total expected years of schooling for children under 18 years of age)<br />
GNIpc: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GNI_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GNI (PPP) per capita">Gross national income at purchasing power parity per capita</a></small>
</p>
<h3><span id="Old_method_.28before_2010_Index.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_method_(before_2010_Index)">Old method (before 2010 Index)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Old method (before 2010 Index)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The HDI combined three dimensions last used in its 2009 Report:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth, as an index of population health and longevity to HDI</li>
<li>Knowledge and education, as measured by the adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate (with two-thirds weighting) and the combined primary, secondary, and tertiary <a href="/wiki/Gross_enrollment_ratio" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross enrollment ratio">gross enrollment ratio</a> (with one-third weighting).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">Standard of living</a>, as indicated by the <a href="/wiki/Natural_logarithm" title="Natural logarithm">natural logarithm</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> <a href="/wiki/Per_capita" title="Per capita">per capita</a> at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>.</li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Human_Development_Index_trends.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Human_Development_Index_trends.svg/280px-Human_Development_Index_trends.svg.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Human_Development_Index_trends.svg/420px-Human_Development_Index_trends.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Human_Development_Index_trends.svg/560px-Human_Development_Index_trends.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1179" data-file-height="1152" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Human_Development_Index_trends.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>HDI trends between 1975 and 2004  <table style="width:100%;">  <tbody><tr> <td valign="top"> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:black; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a></div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; <p>This methodology was used by the UNDP until their 2011 report.
</p><p>The formula defining the HDI is promulgated by the United Nations Development Programme (<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">UNDP</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In general, to transform a raw <a href="/wiki/Variable_(mathematics)" title="Variable (mathematics)">variable</a>, say <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="x"/></span>, into a unit-free <a href="/wiki/Index_(economics)" title="Index (economics)">index</a> between 0 and 1 (which allows different indices to be added together), the following <a href="/wiki/Formula" title="Formula">formula</a> is used:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x{\text{ index}}={\frac {x-a}{b-a}}}">

        </mrow>

        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mi>x</mi>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mi>a</mi>
            </mrow>
            <mrow>
              <mi>b</mi>

<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle a}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>a</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ffd2487510aa438433a2579450ab2b3d557e5edc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.23ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="a"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle b}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>b</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f11423fbb2e967f986e36804a8ae4271734917c3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.998ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="b"/></span> are the <a href="/wiki/Maxima_and_minima" title="Maxima and minima">lowest and highest values</a> the variable <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="x"/></span> can attain, respectively.
</p><p>The Human Development Index (HDI) then represents the uniformly weighted sum with &#x200b;<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>3</sub></span> contributed by each of the following factor indices:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Life_Expectancy_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Life Expectancy Index">Life Expectancy Index</a> = <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {LE-25}{85-25}}}">
  <semantics>

          </mfrac>

<li><a href="/wiki/Education_Index" title="Education Index">Education Index</a> = <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {2}{3}}\times ALI+{\frac {1}{3}}\times GEI}">

<p>Other organizations/companies may include other factors, such as infant mortality, which produces a different HDI.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span id="2017_Human_Development_Index_.282018_report.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017_Human_Development_Index_(2018_report)">2017 Human Development Index (2018 report)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2017 Human Development Index (2018 report)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a></div>
<p>The Human Development Indices and Indicators: 2018 Statistical update by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> was released on 14 September 2018, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Development_Report_2018_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Development_Report_2018-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Development_Report_2018_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Development_Report_2018-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = increase.</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = steady.</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = decrease.</li></ul>

<h3><span id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_.282018_report.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_(2018_report)">Inequality-adjusted HDI (2018 report)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Inequality-adjusted HDI (2018 report)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI)<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account".
</p><p><small>The rankings are not relative to the HDI list above due to the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data (p.&#160;30).</small>
</p>

<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Flag_of_Barbados.svg/23px-Flag_of_Barbados.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Flag_of_Barbados.svg/35px-Flag_of_Barbados.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Flag_of_Barbados.svg/45px-Flag_of_Barbados.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> 0.669</li></ol>
</div>
<p>Countries in the top quartile of HDI ("very high human development" group) with a missing IHDI: <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>.
</p>
<h2><span id="2015_Human_Development_Index_.282016_report.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_Human_Development_Index_(2016_report)">2015 Human Development Index (2016 report)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2015 Human Development Index (2016 report)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a></div>
<p>The 2016 Human Development Report by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> was released on 21 March 2017, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2015. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:<sup id="cite_ref-:0_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = increase.</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = steady.</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = decrease.</li></ul>

<h3><span id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_.282016_report.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_(2016_report)">Inequality-adjusted HDI (2016 report)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Inequality-adjusted HDI (2016 report)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI)<sup id="cite_ref-2016_Complete_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_Complete-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account".
</p><p><small>The rankings are not relative to the HDI list above due to the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data (p.&#160;206).</small>

</div>
<p>Countries in the top quartile of HDI ("very high human development" group) with a missing IHDI: <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>.
</p>
<h2><span id="2014_Human_Development_Index_.282015_report.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_Human_Development_Index_(2015_report)">2014 Human Development Index (2015 report)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2014 Human Development Index (2015 report)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a></div>
<p>The 2015 Human Development Report by the United Nations Development Programme was released on 14 December 2015, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2014. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:<sup id="cite_ref-2015_Complete_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Complete-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Macau_in_Figures,_2015_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_in_Figures,_2015-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dgbas2011_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dgbas2011-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = increase.</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = steady.</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = decrease.</li></ul>

<h3><span id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_.282015_report.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_(2015_report)">Inequality-adjusted HDI  (2015 report)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Inequality-adjusted HDI (2015 report)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI)<sup id="cite_ref-2015_Complete_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Complete-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account".
</p><p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />) represent changes in rank. The rankings are not relative to the HDI list above due to the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data (p.&#160;216).</small>
</p>

<p>Countries in the top quartile of HDI ("very high human development" group) with a missing IHDI: <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>.
</p>
<h2><span id="2013_Human_Development_Index_.282014_report.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_Human_Development_Index_(2014_report)">2013 Human Development Index (2014 report)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2013 Human Development Index (2014 report)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The 2014 Human Development Report by the United Nations Development Programme was released on 24 July 2014 and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2013. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries or regions:<sup id="cite_ref-2014_Complete_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_Complete-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Macau_in_Figures,_2015_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_in_Figures,_2015-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dgbas2011_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dgbas2011-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = increase.</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = steady.</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = decrease.</li></ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_not_included">Countries not included</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Countries not included">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some countries were not included for various reasons, primarily due to the lack of necessary data. The following United Nations Member States were not included in the 2014 report:<sup id="cite_ref-2014_Complete_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_Complete-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_.282014_report.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_(2014_report)">Inequality-adjusted HDI (2014 report)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Inequality-adjusted HDI (2014 report)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI)<sup id="cite_ref-2014_Complete_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_Complete-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account".
</p><p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />) represent changes in rank. The rankings are not relative to the HDI list above due to the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data (p.&#160;168).</small>
</p>

</div>
<p>Countries in the top quartile of HDI ("very high human development" group) with a missing IHDI: <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_top_countries">Past top countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Past top countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The list below displays the top-ranked country from each year of the Human Development Index. <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> has been ranked the highest fourteen times, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> eight times, and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> three times. <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> has been ranked highest twice.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_each_original_HDI">In each original HDI</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: In each original HDI">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The year represents the time period from which the statistics for the index were derived. In parentheses is the year when the report was published.

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_coverage">Geographical coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Geographical coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The HDI has extended its geographical coverage: David Hastings, of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Commission_for_Asia_and_the_Pacific" title="United Nations Economic and Social Commission for Asia and the Pacific">United Nations Economic and Social Commission for Asia and the Pacific</a>, published a report geographically extending the HDI to 230+ economies, whereas the UNDP HDI for 2009 enumerates 182 economies and coverage for the 2010 HDI dropped to 169 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg/220px-Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg/330px-Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg/440px-Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg 2x" data-file-width="850" data-file-height="522" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>HDI vs. <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Human Development Index has been criticized on a number of grounds, including alleged lack of consideration of technological development or contributions to the human civilization, focusing exclusively on national performance and ranking, lack of attention to development from a global perspective, measurement error of the underlying statistics, and on the UNDP's changes in formula which can lead to severe misclassification in the categorisation of "low", "medium", "high" or "very high" human development countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolff_et_al._2011_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolff_et_al._2011-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sources_of_data_error">Sources of data error</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sources of data error">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Economists Hendrik Wolff, Howard Chong and <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Auffhammer" title="Maximilian Auffhammer">Maximilian Auffhammer</a> discuss the HDI from the perspective of data error in the underlying health, education and income statistics used to construct the HDI. They identified three sources of data error which are due to (i) data updating, (ii) formula revisions and (iii) thresholds to classify a country's development status and conclude that 11%, 21% and 34% of all countries can be interpreted as currently misclassified in the development bins due to the three sources of data error, respectively. The authors suggest that the United Nations should discontinue the practice of classifying countries into development bins because: the cut-off values seem arbitrary, can provide incentives for strategic behavior in reporting official statistics, and have the potential to misguide politicians, investors, charity donors and the public who use the HDI at large.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolff_et_al._2011_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolff_et_al._2011-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, the UNDP reacted to the criticism and updated the thresholds to classify nations as low, medium, and high human development countries. In a comment to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> in early January 2011, the Human Development Report Office responded<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> to a 6 January 2011 article in the magazine<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> which discusses the Wolff <i>et al.</i> paper. The Human Development Report Office states that they undertook a systematic revision of the methods used for the calculation of the HDI, and that the new methodology directly addresses the critique by Wolff <i>et al.</i> in that it generates a system for continuously updating the human-development categories whenever formula or data revisions take place.
</p><p>In 2013, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Salvatore_Monni&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Salvatore Monni (page does not exist)">Salvatore Monni</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alessandro_Spaventa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alessandro Spaventa (page does not exist)">Alessandro Spaventa</a> emphasized that in the debate of GDP versus HDI, it is often forgotten that these are both external indicators that prioritize different benchmarks upon which the quantification of societal welfare can be predicated. The larger question is whether it is possible to shift the focus of policy from a battle between competing paradigms to a mechanism for eliciting information on well-being directly from the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Monni_and_Spaventa,_2013_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Monni_and_Spaventa,_2013-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.indiastudychannel.com/resources/141517-New-method-of-calculation-of-Human-Development-Index-HDI.aspx">"New method of calculation of Human Development Index (HDI)"</a>. <i>India Study Channel</i>. 1 June 2011. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20171110171412/http://www.indiastudychannel.com/resources/141517-New-method-of-calculation-of-Human-Development-Index-HDI.aspx">Archived</a> from the original on 10 November 2017<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">19 November</span> 2017</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=India+Study+Channel&amp;rft.atitle=New+method+of+calculation+of+Human+Development+Index+%28HDI%29&amp;rft.date=2011-06-01&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.indiastudychannel.com%2Fresources%2F141517-New-method-of-calculation-of-Human-Development-Index-HDI.aspx&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+Development+Index" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Mean years of schooling (of adults) (years) is a calculation of the average number of years of education received by people ages 25 and older in their lifetime based on education attainment levels of the population converted into years of schooling based on theoretical duration of each level of education attended. Source: <cite class="citation journal"><a href="/wiki/Robert_Barro" title="Robert Barro">Barro, R. J.</a>; Lee, J.-W. (2010). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nber.org/papers/w15902">"A New Data Set of Educational Attainment in the World, 1950–2010"</a>. <i>NBER Working Paper No. 15902</i>. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.3386%2Fw15902">10.3386/w15902</a>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110807191234/http://www.nber.org/papers/w15902">Archived</a> from the original on 7 August 2011<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">29 July</span> 2011</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=NBER+Working+Paper+No.+15902&amp;rft.atitle=A+New+Data+Set+of+Educational+Attainment+in+the+World%2C+1950%E2%80%932010&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.3386%2Fw15902&amp;rft.aulast=Barro&amp;rft.aufirst=R.+J.&amp;rft.au=Lee%2C+J.-W.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.nber.org%2Fpapers%2Fw15902&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+Development+Index" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">(ESYI is a calculation of the number of years a child is expected to attend school, or university, including the years spent on repetition. It is the sum of the age-specific enrollment ratios for primary, secondary, post-secondary non-tertiary and tertiary education and is calculated assuming the prevailing patterns of age-specific enrollment rates were to stay the same throughout the child's life. Expected years of schooling is capped at 18 years. (Source: UNESCO Institute for Statistics (2010). Correspondence on education indicators. March. Montreal.)</span>
</li>

</li>

<li id="cite_note-Macau_in_Figures,_2015-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Macau_in_Figures,_2015_19-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Macau_in_Figures,_2015_19-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The UN does not calculate the HDI of Macau. The government of Macau calculates its own HDI.<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dsec.gov.mo/getAttachment/0d4efddf-7ad1-400c-ae84-7137d9c9df9f/E_MN_PUB_2015_Y.aspx">Macau in Figures, 2015</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150923220838/http://www.dsec.gov.mo/getAttachment/0d4efddf-7ad1-400c-ae84-7137d9c9df9f/E_MN_PUB_2015_Y.aspx">Archived</a> 23 September 2015 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a></span>

<li id="cite_note-dgbas1-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-dgbas1_23-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-dgbas1_23-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The UN <a href="/wiki/China_and_the_United_Nations" title="China and the United Nations">does not recognize</a> the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (<a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>) as a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a>. The HDI report does not include Taiwan as part of the People's Republic of China when calculating China's figures. Taiwan's government calculated its HDI to be 0.882, based on 2010 new methodology of UNDP. <cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dgbas.gov.tw/public/Data/491716362790WG0X9I.pdf">"2011中華民國人類發展指數 (HDI)"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> (in Chinese). <li><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20080216013844/http://hdr.undp.org/en/media/hdr_20072008_tech_note_1.pdf">"Technical note explaining the definition of the HDI"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Technical+note+explaining+the+definition+of+the+HDI&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fweb.archive.org%2Fweb%2F20080216013844%2Fhttp%3A%2F%2Fhdr.undp.org%2Fen%2Fmedia%2Fhdr_20072008_tech_note_1.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+Development+Index" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/>&#160;<span style="font-size:85%;">(5.54&#160;MB)</span></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/web/products-eurostat-news/-/DDN-20170306-1?inheritRedirect=true&amp;redirect=%2Feurostat%2Fhome">New demographic datasets by 'Human Development Index (HDI)’</a></li>
<li>An independent <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.humansecurityindex.org/?page_id=204">HDI</a> covering 232 countries, formulated along the lines of the traditional (pre-2010) approach.</li></ul>
